This reminds me of a Audi S2 project we did with my father. We installed ABT bodykit to it and spent 6 months buildiing it. During first test drive oil spilled with high pressure and it set on fire. The whole front burnt. All the rubber pipes and lines and the body kit which was glass fiber almost completely destroyed. Most devastating situation in my life for sure :D. After 2 weeks of depression we started over and after 3 months we did a new test drive with extinguisher on the back seat and it was perfect. In any project the more you have downfall the more better it feels when it's complete. I think the most used sentence i have used is "i give up" but i never had. I think this car hobby is some sort of masochism but it just feels so good in the end. :) I hope everything works out for you!

"Deckel" in german usually just means "lid" for bottles, etc. For the hood/bonnet of a car we usually say "Motorhaube" (quite literally "engine bonnet", I guess). We actually call it (hood / bonnet) "Motorhaube" (translated word by word it would be somthing like "enignehood") - the word "Deckel" is a more general term for some sort of topper (it can also be used to refer to a bottlecap or the lid of a jar), so I suppose "Deckel" also works, but I'm not sure if everyone would understand what you are talking about if you werent holding a bonnet in your hands.

It`s not called "Deckel"!  It's a "Haube" more precise a "Motorhaube" if you have an engine in the front or in this case a "Fronthaube" if the engine is in the back.
Cheers from Germany! Little PSA: It's called Deckel, if it's covering the trunk, but it's called Haube oder Motorhaube, if it's covering the engine.

As a german, its kinda funny to hear "Or Deckel if you're german", since "Deckel" refers more to something like a lid of a glass, or a bowl. With the hood, the original word is "Motorhaube" (which on the other hand consists of "Motor" (=engine) and "Haube" (=cap, cover), so technically the hood is the enginecap in german :D (which is funny, since it could as well be "enginecover", which in english usually is the piece of plastic in your enginebay covering the engine.

The reason it smoked is because the last time it was ran, the engine was revved up and sent oil to the turbo for what it thought was going to be a run. When it idled down, the oil sat in the turbo and then burns off on next start. All turbos will do it which is why they used to come with timers to let the car idle for 2 minutes to cycle the oil to help cool the turbskies

@Mat Armstrong: @18:03 Already noticed it in your Porsche video but forgot to comment: The German word for bonnet is "Motorhaube". The German word "Decke" means both "blanket" and "ceiling". I suppose the Porsche engineers were just referring to the top/bottom or rather up/down alignment of the car parts with a weird wording like "Decke"/"Boden" as in ceiling. Not as literal blanket covering the engine. ;)

Bonnet means "Motorhaube" (which translates to "engine hood")  in German, not "Deckel". They wrote "Deckel" on the Porsche, because there is no engine underneath it but a trunk and a trunk lid is a "Kofferraumdeckel" in German. That is where the word "Deckel" comes from.
